				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Amazon.com_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com Inc.">Amazon.com Inc.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Amazon.com, Inc.</b><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>), is an American multinational conglomerate technology company based in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, with 750,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> It focuses on <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Digital_streaming" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital streaming">digital streaming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>. It is considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_tech_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four tech companies">Big Four tech companies</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It has been referred to as "one of the most influential economic and cultural forces in the world."<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$62.060 billion</span> (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" Depository">Book Depository</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/ComiXology" title="ComiXology">ComiXology</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Goodreads" title="Goodreads">Goodreads</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Graphiq" href="https://www.amazon.com">www<wbr></wbr>.amazon<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-ar2017_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar2017-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BS_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BS-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sos_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sos-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Amazon is known for its disruption of well-established industries through technological innovation and mass scale.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Online_marketplace" title="Online marketplace">online marketplace</a>, <a href="/wiki/AI_assistant" class="mw-redirect" title="AI assistant">AI assistant</a> provider, and <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> platform<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> as measured by <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Amazon is the <a href="/wiki/Largest_Internet_company_by_revenue" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest Internet company by revenue">largest Internet company by revenue</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> It is the second <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_employers_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="List of largest employers in the United States">largest private employer in the United States</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and one of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_most_valuable_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="World's most valuable companies">world's most valuable companies</a>.
</p><p>Amazon was founded by <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bellevue,_Washington" title="Bellevue, Washington">Bellevue, Washington</a>, in July 1994. The company initially started as an online marketplace for books but later expanded to sell electronics, software, video games, apparel, furniture, food, toys, and jewelry. In 2015, Amazon surpassed <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> as the most valuable retailer in the United States by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2017, Amazon acquired <a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods_Market" title="Whole Foods Market">Whole Foods Market</a> for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>13.4 billion, which vastly increased Amazon's presence as a brick-and-mortar retailer.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In 2018, Bezos announced that its two-day delivery service, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Prime" title="Amazon Prime">Amazon Prime</a>, had surpassed 100 million subscribers worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>Amazon distributes downloads and streaming of <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Video">video</a>, music, and <a href="/wiki/Audible.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Audible.com">audiobooks</a> through its <a href="/wiki/Prime_Video" title="Prime Video">Prime Video</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Music" title="Amazon Music">Amazon Music</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Audible_(store)" title="Audible (store)">Audible</a> subsidiaries. Amazon also has a publishing arm, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Publishing" title="Amazon Publishing">Amazon Publishing</a>, a film and television studio, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Studios" title="Amazon Studios">Amazon Studios</a>, and a cloud computing subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/AWS" class="mw-redirect" title="AWS">Amazon Web Services</a>. It produces <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a> including <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Kindle" title="Amazon Kindle">Kindle</a> <a href="/wiki/E-reader" title="E-reader">e-readers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kindle_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kindle Fire">Fire</a> <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fire_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire TV">Fire TV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Echo" title="Amazon Echo">Echo</a> devices. In addition, Amazon acquisitions include <a href="/wiki/Ring_Inc." title="Ring Inc.">Ring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a>, Whole Foods Market, and <a href="/wiki/IMDb" title="IMDb">IMDb</a>. Among various controversies, the company has been <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Amazon" title="Criticism of Amazon">criticized</a> for technological surveillance overreach,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> a hyper-competitive and demanding work culture,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">tax avoidance</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fortune_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-26">[26]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-competitive_practices" title="Anti-competitive practices">anti-competitive practices.</a><sup id="cite_ref-:6_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-baum_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baum-28">[28]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Amazon" title="History of Amazon">History of Amazon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_Hyderabad_campus.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Amazon_Hyderabad_campus.jpg/220px-Amazon_Hyderabad_campus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="2160"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Amazon_Hyderabad_campus.jpg/220px-Amazon_Hyderabad_campus.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_Hyderabad_campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The company's largest campus outside of the US was inaugurated in <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> in September 2019.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a> founded Amazon in July 1994. He chose <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> because of technical talent as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> is located there.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In May 1997, the organization went <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public</a>. The company began selling music and videos in 1998, at which time it began operations internationally by acquiring online sellers of books in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. The following year, the organization also sold video games, consumer electronics, home-improvement items, software, games, and toys in addition to other items.
</p><p>In 2002, the corporation started <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a> (AWS), which provided data on Web site popularity, Internet traffic patterns and other statistics for marketers and developers. In 2006, the organization grew its AWS portfolio when <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Elastic_Compute_Cloud" title="Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud">Elastic Compute Cloud</a> (EC2), which rents computer processing power as well as <a href="/wiki/Simple_Storage_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Simple Storage Service">Simple Storage Service</a> (S3), that rents data storage via the Internet, were made available. That same year, the company started<i> Fulfillment by Amazon </i>which managed the inventory of individuals and small companies selling their belongings through the company internet site. In 2012, Amazon bought <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Robotics" title="Amazon Robotics">Kiva Systems</a> to automate its inventory-management business, purchasing <a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods_Market" title="Whole Foods Market">Whole Foods Market</a> supermarket chain five years later in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jeff_Bezos_2016.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jeff_Bezos_2016.jpg/170px-Jeff_Bezos_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="609" data-file-height="819"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 170px;height: 229px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Jeff_Bezos_2016.jpg/170px-Jeff_Bezos_2016.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="170" data-height="229" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jeff_Bezos_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amazon founder <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a> in 2016</div></div></div>
<p>As of November 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_(company)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the board of directors is:<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a>, President, CEO, and Chairman</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rosalind_Brewer" title="Rosalind Brewer">Rosalind Brewer</a>, Group President, and COO, <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jamie_Gorelick" title="Jamie Gorelick">Jamie Gorelick</a>, partner, <a href="/wiki/Wilmer_Cutler_Pickering_Hale_and_Dorr" title="Wilmer Cutler Pickering Hale and Dorr">Wilmer Cutler Pickering Hale, and Dorr</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_P._Huttenlocher" title="Daniel P. Huttenlocher">Daniel P. Huttenlocher</a>, Dean of the Schwarzman College of Computing at the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Judy_McGrath" title="Judy McGrath">Judy McGrath</a>, former CEO, <a href="/wiki/MTV_Networks" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Networks">MTV Networks</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indra_Nooyi" title="Indra Nooyi">Indra Nooyi</a>, former CEO, <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jon_Rubinstein" title="Jon Rubinstein">Jon Rubinstein</a>, former Chairman, and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc." title="Palm, Inc.">Palm, Inc.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Ryder" title="Thomas O. Ryder">Thomas O. Ryder</a>, former Chairman, and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Reader%27s_Digest_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Reader's Digest Association">Reader's Digest Association</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patty_Stonesifer" title="Patty Stonesifer">Patty Stonesifer</a>, President, and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Table" title="Martha's Table">Martha's Table</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wendell_P._Weeks" class="mw-redirect" title="Wendell P. Weeks">Wendell P. Weeks</a>, Chairman, President, and CEO, <a href="/wiki/Corning_Inc." title="Corning Inc.">Corning Inc.</a></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchant_partnerships">Merchant partnerships</span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>In 2000, U.S. toy retailer <a href="/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us" title='Toys "R" Us'>Toys "R" Us</a> entered into a 10-year agreement with Amazon, valued at $50 million per year plus a cut of sales, under which Toys "R" Us would be the exclusive supplier of toys and baby products on the service, and the chain's website would redirect to Amazon's Toys &amp; Games category. In 2004, Toys "R" Us sued Amazon, claiming that because of a perceived lack of variety in Toys "R" Us stock, Amazon had knowingly allowed third-party sellers to offer items on the service in categories that Toys "R" Us had been granted exclusivity. In 2006, a court ruled in favor of Toys "R" Us, giving it the right to unwind its agreement with Amazon and establish its own independent e-commerce website. The company was later awarded $51 million in damages.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p><p>In 2001, Amazon entered into a similar agreement with <a href="/wiki/Borders_Group" title="Borders Group">Borders Group</a>, under which Amazon would comanage Borders.com as a co-branded service.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Borders pulled out of the arrangement in 2007, with plans to also launch its own online store.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p><p>On October 18, 2011, Amazon.com announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> for the exclusive digital rights to many popular comics, including <i><a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Green_Lantern" title="Green Lantern">Green Lantern</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sandman_(Vertigo)" title="The Sandman (Vertigo)">The Sandman</a>,</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Watchmen" title="Watchmen">Watchmen</a></i>. The partnership has caused well-known bookstores like Barnes &amp; Noble to remove these titles from their shelves.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2013, Amazon announced a partnership with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> to begin delivering orders on Sundays. The service, included in Amazon's standard shipping rates, initiated in metropolitan areas of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="New York, New York">New York</a> because of the high-volume and inability to deliver in a timely way, with plans to expand into <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a> by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2017, <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> confirmed a "pilot" partnership with Amazon to sell goods directly on the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>As of October 11, 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_(company)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/AmazonFresh" title="AmazonFresh">AmazonFresh</a> sold a range of <a href="/wiki/Booths_Supermarkets" class="mw-redirect" title="Booths Supermarkets">Booths</a> branded products for home delivery in selected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2017, Amazon ventured with one of its sellers JV Appario Retail owned by Patni Group which has recorded a total income of US$ 104.44 million (<a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">₹</a> 759 <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore">crore</a>) in financial year 2017–18.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2018, Amazon reached an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> to sell selected products through the service, via the company and selected Apple Authorized Resellers. As a result of this partnership, only Apple Authorized Resellers may sell Apple products on Amazon effective January 4, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Amazon_products_and_services" title="List of Amazon products and services">List of Amazon products and services</a></div>
<p>Amazon.com's product lines available at its website include several media (<a href="/wiki/Book" title="Book">books</a>, DVDs, music CDs, <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">videotapes</a> and software), apparel, baby products, <a href="/wiki/Consumer_electronics" title="Consumer electronics">consumer electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cosmetics" title="Cosmetics">beauty products</a>, gourmet food, groceries, health and personal-care items, industrial &amp; scientific supplies, kitchen items, <a href="/wiki/Jewelry" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewelry">jewelry</a>, watches, lawn and garden items, musical instruments, <a href="/wiki/Sports_equipment" title="Sports equipment">sporting goods</a>, tools, automotive items and toys &amp; games.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In August 2019, Amazon applied to have a liquor store in San Francisco, CA as a means to ship beer and alcohol within the city.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Amazon has separate retail websites for some countries and also offers international shipping of some of its products to certain other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p><p>Amazon.com has a number of products and services available, including:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/AmazonFresh" title="AmazonFresh">AmazonFresh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Prime" title="Amazon Prime">Amazon Prime</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Alexa" title="Amazon Alexa">Alexa</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Appstore" title="Amazon Appstore">Appstore</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Drive" title="Amazon Drive">Amazon Drive</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Echo" title="Amazon Echo">Echo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Kindle" title="Amazon Kindle">Kindle</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kindle_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kindle Fire">Fire tablets</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Fire_TV" title="Amazon Fire TV">Fire TV</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Video">Video</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kindle_Store" title="Kindle Store">Kindle Store</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Music" title="Amazon Music">Music</a></li>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Amazon_locations" title="List of Amazon locations">List of Amazon locations</a></div>
<p>Amazon owns over 40 subsidiaries, including <a href="/wiki/Zappos" title="Zappos">Zappos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shopbop" title="Shopbop">Shopbop</a>, Diapers.com, Kiva Systems (now <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Robotics" title="Amazon Robotics">Amazon Robotics</a>), <a href="/wiki/Audible_(store)" title="Audible (store)">Audible</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goodreads" title="Goodreads">Goodreads</a>, Teachstreet, <a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a> and <a href="/wiki/IMDb" title="IMDb">IMDb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="A9.com">A9.com</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/A9.com" title="A9.com">A9.com</a>, a company focused on researching and building innovative <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>, has been a subsidiary since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Amazon_Maritime">Amazon Maritime</span></h3>
<p>Amazon Maritime, Inc. holds a <a href="/wiki/Federal_Maritime_Commission" title="Federal Maritime Commission">Federal Maritime Commission</a> license to operate as a <a href="/wiki/NVOCC" class="mw-redirect" title="NVOCC">non-vessel-owning common carrier</a> (NVOCC), which enables the company to manage its own shipments from China into the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Annapurna_Labs">Annapurna Labs</span></h3>
<p>In January 2015, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a> acquired <a href="/wiki/Annapurna_Labs" title="Annapurna Labs">Annapurna Labs</a>, an Israel-based microelectronics company reputedly for US$350–370M.<sup id="cite_ref-reut_Amaz_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reut_Amaz-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-extr_Amaz_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extr_Amaz-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Audible.com">Audible.com</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Audible.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Audible.com">Audible.com</a> is a seller and producer of spoken audio entertainment, information and educational programming on the Internet. Audible sells digital <a href="/wiki/Audiobooks" class="mw-redirect" title="Audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, radio and TV programs and audio versions of magazines and newspapers. Through its production arm, Audible Studios, Audible has also become the world's largest producer of downloadable audiobooks. On January 31, 2008, Amazon announced it would buy Audible for about $300 million. The deal closed in March 2008 and Audible became a subsidiary of Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Beijing_Century_Joyo_Courier_Services">Beijing Century Joyo Courier Services</span></h3>
<p>Beijing Century Joyo Courier Services is a subsidiary of Amazon and it applied for a <a href="/wiki/Freight_forwarder" title="Freight forwarder">freight forwarding</a> license with the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Maritime_Commission" title="Federal Maritime Commission">US Maritime Commission</a>. Amazon is also building out its logistics in <a href="/wiki/Trucking_industry_in_the_United_States" title="Trucking industry in the United States">trucking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_freight" class="mw-redirect" title="Air freight">air freight</a> to potentially compete with <a href="/wiki/United_Parcel_Service" title="United Parcel Service">UPS</a> and <a href="/wiki/FedEx" title="FedEx">FedEx</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Brilliance_Audio">Brilliance Audio</span></h3>
<p>Brilliance Audio is an audiobook publisher founded in 1984 by Michael Snodgrass in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Haven,_Michigan" title="Grand Haven, Michigan">Grand Haven, Michigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brilliance_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brilliance-56">[56]</a></sup> The company produced its first 8 audio titles in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-brilliance_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brilliance-56">[56]</a></sup> The company was purchased by Amazon in 2007 for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gigaom_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gigaom-58">[58]</a></sup> At the time of the acquisition, Brilliance was producing 12–15 new titles a month.<sup id="cite_ref-gigaom_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gigaom-58">[58]</a></sup> It operates as an independent company within Amazon.
</p><p>In 1984, Brilliance Audio invented a technique for recording twice as much on the same cassette.<sup id="cite_ref-blake_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blake-59">[59]</a></sup> The technique involved recording on each of the two channels of each stereo track.<sup id="cite_ref-blake_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blake-59">[59]</a></sup> It has been credited with revolutionizing the burgeoning audiobook market in the mid-1980s since it made unabridged books affordable.<sup id="cite_ref-blake_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blake-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="ComiXology">ComiXology</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/ComiXology" title="ComiXology">ComiXology</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud</a>-based digital comics platform with over 200 million comic downloads as of September 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_(company)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. It offers a selection of more than 40,000 comic books and graphic novels across Android, iOS, Fire OS and Windows 8 devices and over a web browser. Amazon bought the company in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="CreateSpace">CreateSpace</span></h3>
<p>CreateSpace, which offers self-publishing services for independent content creators, publishers, film studios, and music labels, became a subsidiary in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Eero">Eero</span></h3>
<p>Eero is a company that manufactures mesh-capable routers. The company was founded in 2015 and is based in San Francisco. Amazon announced it would buy Eero in 2019.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Goodreads">Goodreads</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Goodreads" title="Goodreads">Goodreads</a> is a "<a href="/wiki/Social_cataloging" class="mw-redirect" title="Social cataloging">social cataloging</a>" website founded in December 2006 and launched in January 2007 by Otis Chandler, a software engineer, and entrepreneur, and Elizabeth Chandler. The website allows individuals to freely search Goodreads' extensive user-populated database of books, annotations, and reviews. Users can sign up and register books to generate library catalogs and reading lists. They can also create their own groups of book suggestions and discussions. In December 2007, the site had over 650,000 members and over 10 million books had been added. Amazon bought the company in March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_Navigator">Health Navigator</span></h3>
<p>In October 2019, Amazon finalized the acquisition of Health Navigator, a startup developing <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">APIs</a> for online health services. The startup will form part of Amazon Care, which is the company's employee healthcare service. This follows the 2018 purchase of <a href="/wiki/PillPack" title="PillPack">PillPack</a> for under $1 billion, which has also been included into Amazon Care.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Junglee">Junglee</span></h3>
<p>Junglee is a former online shopping service provided by Amazon that enabled customers to search for products from online and offline retailers in India. Junglee started off as a virtual database that was used to extract information off the internet and deliver it to enterprise applications. As it progressed, Junglee started to use its database technology to create a single window marketplace on the internet by making every item from every supplier available for purchase. Web shoppers could locate, compare and transact millions of products from across the Internet shopping mall through one window.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p><p>Amazon acquired Junglee in 1998, and the website Junglee.com was launched in India in February 2012<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> as a comparison-shopping website. It curated and enabled searching for a diverse variety of products such as clothing, electronics, toys, jewelry and video games, among others, across thousands of online and offline sellers. Millions of products are browse-able, whereby the client selects a price, and then they are directed to a seller. In November 2017, Amazon closed down Junglee.com and the former domain currently redirects to Amazon India.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Kuiper_Systems">Kuiper Systems<span id="Project_Kuiper"></span></span></h3>
<p>Amazon announced in April 2019 that they would fund and deploy a large <a href="/wiki/Broadband" title="Broadband">broadband</a> <a href="/wiki/Satellite_internet_constellation" title="Satellite internet constellation">satellite internet constellation</a> called "<b>Project Kuiper</b>".<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc20190404_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc20190404-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sn20190404_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sn20190404-69">[69]</a></sup> It is expected to take up to a decade to fully deploy all 3,236 satellites planned for the full constellation in order to provide internet to "tens of millions of people who lack basic access to broadband internet."<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc20190404_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc20190404-68">[68]</a></sup> Amazon has not announced if they intend to sell <a href="/wiki/Broadband" title="Broadband">broadband</a> service directly to consumers, but they will "offer broadband service through partnerships with other companies."<sup id="cite_ref-ars20190708_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars20190708-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>The satellites will use an orbit with a height between 590 and 630 km (370 and 390 mi).<sup id="cite_ref-bb20090705_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bb20090705-71">[71]</a></sup> Kuiper will work in concert with Amazon's previously announced large network of 12 satellite ground station facilities (the "<b>AWS Ground Station unit</b>") announced in November 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-cnbc20181127_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc20181127-72">[72]</a></sup> Amazon filed communications license documents with the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Regulatory_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulatory authority">regulatory authorities</a> the <a href="/wiki/FCC" class="mw-redirect" title="FCC">FCC</a> in July 2019, which included information that the wholly owned Amazon subsidiary that intended to deploy the satellite constellation was Kuiper Systems LLC, based in Seattle, Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-fcc20190704_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fcc20190704-73">[73]</a></sup>  The Kuiper System will consist of 3,236 satellites operating in 98 <a href="/wiki/Orbital_plane_(astronomy)" title="Orbital plane (astronomy)">orbital planes</a> in three <a href="/wiki/Orbital_shell_(spaceflight)" title="Orbital shell (spaceflight)">orbital shells</a>, one each at 590 kilometers (370 mi), 610 km (380 mi), and 630 km (390 mi) <a href="/wiki/Orbital_altitude" class="mw-redirect" title="Orbital altitude">orbital altitude</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sn20190708_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sn20190708-74">[74]</a></sup>  The Kuiper System includes high-performance satellites, terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Gateway_(telecommunications)" title="Gateway (telecommunications)">gateways</a>, internetworking technologies, and a range of customer terminals."<sup id="cite_ref-fcc20190704_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fcc20190704-73">[73]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2019, information became public that Amazon is asking the FCC to waive requirements that <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a> and <a href="/wiki/OneWeb" title="OneWeb">OneWeb</a> had to follow in order to get their large satellite internet constellations licensed.<sup id="cite_ref-vice201912_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vice201912-75">[75]</a></sup>  The FCC has not yet ruled on the request.
</p><p>The president of Kuiper Systems is Rajeev Badyal, a former vice president of <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">SpaceX</a>'s <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Starlink" class="mw-redirect" title="SpaceX Starlink">Starlink</a> satellite internet constellation.<sup id="cite_ref-ars20190708_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars20190708-70">[70]</a></sup> During 2020 the Kuiper team will move to a larger R&amp;D facility in <a href="/wiki/Redmond,_Washington" title="Redmond, Washington">Redmond, Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sn-20191218_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sn-20191218-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Lab126">Lab126</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Lab126" title="Amazon Lab126">Amazon Lab126</a></div>
<p>Lab126, developers of integrated consumer electronics such as the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Kindle" title="Amazon Kindle">Kindle</a>, became a subsidiary in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ring">Ring</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ring_Inc." title="Ring Inc.">Ring Inc.</a></div>
<p>Ring is a home automation company founded by Jamie Siminoff in 2013. It is primarily known for its WiFi powered <a href="/wiki/Smart_doorbell" title="Smart doorbell">smart doorbells</a>, but manufactures other devices such as security cameras. Amazon bought Ring for $1 billion USD in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Shelfari">Shelfari</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shelfari" title="Shelfari">Shelfari</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Social_cataloging" class="mw-redirect" title="Social cataloging">social cataloging</a> website for books. Shelfari users built virtual bookshelves of the titles which they owned or had read and they could rate, review, <a href="/wiki/Tag_(metadata)" title="Tag (metadata)">tag</a> and discuss their books. Users could also create groups that other members could join, create discussions and talk about books, or other topics. Recommendations could be sent to friends on the site for what books to read. Amazon bought the company in August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-63">[63]</a></sup> Shelfari continued to function as an independent book social network within the Amazon until January 2016, when Amazon announced that it would be merging Shelfari with Goodreads and closing down Shelfari.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Souq">Souq</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Souq.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Souq.com">Souq.com</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Souq.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Souq.com">Souq.com</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Ecommerce_platform" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecommerce platform">E-Commerce platform</a> in the Middle East based in Dubai, United Arab Emirates. On March 28, 2017, Amazon confirmed it would be acquiring Souq.com for $580 million.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Souq.com is now a subsidiary of Amazon, and acts as Amazon's arm into the Middle East region.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Twitch">Twitch</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:E3_%E2%80%93_2014_(23113432796).jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/E3_%E2%80%93_2014_%2823113432796%29.jpg/220px-E3_%E2%80%93_2014_%2823113432796%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 124px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/E3_%E2%80%93_2014_%2823113432796%29.jpg/220px-E3_%E2%80%93_2014_%2823113432796%29.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="124" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:E3_%E2%80%93_2014_(23113432796).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">Electronic Entertainment Expo</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Twitch_(service)" title="Twitch (service)">Twitch</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Live_streaming" title="Live streaming">live streaming</a> platform for video, primarily oriented towards video gaming content. The service was first established as a spin-off of a general-interest streaming service known as <a href="/wiki/Justin.tv" title="Justin.tv">Justin.tv</a>. Its prominence was eclipsed by that of Twitch, and Justin.tv was eventually shut down by its parent company in August 2014 in order to focus exclusively on Twitch.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Later that month, Twitch was acquired by Amazon for $970 million.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Through Twitch, Amazon also owns <a href="/wiki/Curse,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Curse, Inc.">Curse, Inc.</a>, an operator of video gaming communities and a provider of <a href="/wiki/VoIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VoIP">VoIP</a> services for gaming.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Since the acquisition, Twitch began to sell games directly through the platform,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and began offering special features for Amazon Prime subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>The site's rapid growth had been boosted primarily by the prominence of major <a href="/wiki/Esports" title="Esports">esports</a> competitions on the service, leading <a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> senior esports editor Rod Breslau to have described the service as "the <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> of esports".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_(company)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the service had over 1.5 million broadcasters and 100 million monthly viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Whole_Foods_Market">Whole Foods Market</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Whole_Foods_Market_Cranbrook_Village_Ann_Arbor_Michigan.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Whole_Foods_Market_Cranbrook_Village_Ann_Arbor_Michigan.JPG/220px-Whole_Foods_Market_Cranbrook_Village_Ann_Arbor_Michigan.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Whole_Foods_Market_Cranbrook_Village_Ann_Arbor_Michigan.JPG/220px-Whole_Foods_Market_Cranbrook_Village_Ann_Arbor_Michigan.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Whole_Foods_Market_Cranbrook_Village_Ann_Arbor_Michigan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods_Market" title="Whole Foods Market">Whole Foods Market</a> store in <a href="/wiki/Ann_Arbor,_Michigan" title="Ann Arbor, Michigan">Ann Arbor, Michigan</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Whole_Foods_Market" title="Whole Foods Market">Whole Foods Market</a> is an American <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarket</a> <a href="/wiki/Chain_store" title="Chain store">chain</a> exclusively featuring foods without artificial preservatives, colors, flavors, sweeteners, and hydrogenated fats.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p><p>On August 23, 2017, it was reported that the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> approved the merger between Amazon.com and Whole Foods Market.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The following day it was announced that the deal would be closed on August 28, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Supply_chain">Supply chain</span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>Amazon first launched its distribution network in 1997 with two fulfillment centers in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">New Castle, Delaware</a>. Amazon has several types of distribution facilities consisting of crossdock centers, fulfillment centers, sortation centers, delivery stations, Prime now hubs, and Prime air hubs. There are 75 fulfillment centers and 25 sortation centers with over 125,000 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Employees are responsible for five basic tasks: unpacking and inspecting incoming goods; placing goods in storage and recording their location; picking goods from their computer recorded locations to make up an individual shipment; sorting and packing orders; and shipping. A computer that records the location of goods and maps out routes for pickers plays a key role: employees carry hand-held computers which communicate with the central computer and monitor their rate of progress. Some warehouses are partially automated with systems built by <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Robotics" title="Amazon Robotics">Amazon Robotics</a>.
</p>

</td>
<td>November 2017
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Reviews">Reviews</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Amazon#Amazon_reviews" title="Criticism of Amazon">Criticism of Amazon § Amazon reviews</a></div>
<p>Amazon allows users to submit reviews to the web page of each product. Reviewers must rate the product on a <a href="/wiki/Rating_scale" title="Rating scale">rating scale</a> from one to five stars. Amazon provides a badging option for reviewers which indicate the real name of the reviewer (based on confirmation of a credit card account) or which indicate that the reviewer is one of the top reviewers by popularity. Customers may comment or vote on the reviews, indicating whether they found a review helpful to them. If a review is given enough "helpful" hits, it appears on the front page of the product. In 2010, Amazon was reported as being the largest single source of Internet consumer reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>When publishers asked Bezos why Amazon would publish negative reviews, he defended the practice by claiming that Amazon.com was "taking a different approach ... we want to make every book available—the good, the bad and the ugly ... to let truth loose".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>There have been cases of positive reviews being written and posted by <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> companies on behalf of their clients<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> and instances of writers using pseudonyms to leave negative reviews of their rivals' works.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_search">Content search</span></h3>
<p>"Search Inside the Book" is a feature which allows customers to search for keywords in the full text of many books in the catalog.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The feature started with 120,000 titles (or 33 million pages of text) on October 23, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> There are about 300,000 books in the program. Amazon has cooperated with around 130 <a href="/wiki/Publisher" class="mw-redirect" title="Publisher">publishers</a> to allow users to perform these searches.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>To avoid copyright violations, Amazon does not return the computer-readable text of the book. Instead, it returns a picture of the matching page, instructs the web browser to disable printing and puts limits on the number of pages in a book a single user can access. Additionally, customers can purchase online access to some of the same books via the "Amazon Upgrade" program.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Third-party_sellers">Third-party sellers</span></h3>
<p>Amazon derives many of its sales (around 40% in 2008) from third-party sellers who sell products on Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Associates receive a commission for referring customers to Amazon by placing links to Amazon on their websites if the referral results in a sale. Worldwide, Amazon has "over 900,000 members" in its affiliate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In the middle of 2014, the Amazon Affiliate Program is used by 1.2% of all websites and it is the second most popular advertising network after Google Ads.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> It is frequently used by websites and non-profits to provide a way for supporters to earn them a commission.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Amazon reported over 1.3 million sellers sold products through Amazon's websites in 2007. Unlike <a href="/wiki/EBay.com" class="mw-redirect" title="EBay.com">eBay</a>, Amazon sellers do not have to maintain separate payment accounts; all payments are handled by Amazon.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Associates can access the Amazon catalog directly on their websites by using the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a> (AWS) <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> service. A new affiliate product, aStore, allows Associates to embed a subset of Amazon products within another website, or linked to another website. In June 2010, Amazon Seller Product Suggestions was launched (rumored to be internally called "Project Genesis") to provide more transparency to sellers by recommending specific products to third-party sellers to sell on Amazon. Products suggested are based on customers' browsing history.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In 2019, Amazon launched a bigger local online store in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> to expand its product selection in the face of intensifying competition with competitors in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2019 the 3rd U.S. City Court of Appeals in Philadelphia ruled that Amazon can be held accountable for faulty third-party sales.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The decision ran counter to a past lower court ruling that had favored Amazon. Heather Oberdorf had sued the company in 2016 over a dog leash that snapped, causing permanent loss of vision in one eye. If upheld, the decision would expose Amazon and similar platform businesses to strict liability lawsuits for defective products, which represents a major change in the law.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The panel sent the case back to the lower court, to decide whether the leash was actually defective.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Amazon_sales_rank">Amazon sales rank</span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>The Amazon sales rank (ASR) provides an indication of the popularity of a product sold on any Amazon locale. It is a relative indicator of popularity that is updated hourly. Effectively, it is a "best sellers list" for the millions of products stocked by Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-amazon_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amazon-115">[115]</a></sup> While the ASR has no direct effect on the sales of a product, it is used by Amazon to determine which products to include in its bestsellers lists.<sup id="cite_ref-amazon_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amazon-115">[115]</a></sup> Products that appear in these lists enjoy additional exposure on the Amazon website and this may lead to an increase in sales. In particular, products that experience large jumps (up or down) in their sales ranks may be included within Amazon's lists of "movers and shakers"; such a listing provides additional exposure that might lead to an increase in sales.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> For competitive reasons, Amazon does not release actual sales figures to the public. However, Amazon has now begun to release <a href="/wiki/Point_of_sale" title="Point of sale">point of sale</a> data via the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_BookScan" title="Nielsen BookScan">Nielsen BookScan</a> service to verified authors.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> While the ASR has been the source of much speculation by publishers, manufacturers, and marketers, Amazon itself does not release the details of its sales rank calculation algorithm. Some companies have analyzed Amazon sales data to generate sales estimates based on the ASR,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> though Amazon states:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Please keep in mind that our sales rank figures are simply meant to be a guide of general interest for the customer and not definitive sales information for publishers—we assume you have this information regularly from your distribution sources</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Amazon.com Help<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Multi-level_sales_strategy">Multi-level sales strategy</span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>Amazon employs a multi-level e-commerce strategy. Amazon started by focusing on business-to-consumer relationships between itself and its customers and business-to-business relationships between itself and its suppliers and then moved to facilitate customer-to-customer with the Amazon marketplace which acts as an intermediary to facilitate transactions. The company lets anyone sell nearly anything using its platform. In addition to an affiliate program that lets anyone post Amazon links and earn a commission on click-through sales, there is now a program which lets those affiliates build entire websites based on Amazon's platform.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p><p>Some other large e-commerce sellers use Amazon to sell their products in addition to selling them through their own websites. The sales are processed through Amazon.com and end up at individual sellers for processing and order fulfillment and Amazon leases space for these retailers. Small sellers of used and new goods go to Amazon Marketplace to offer goods at a fixed price.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p><p>Amazon also employs the use of <a href="/wiki/Drop_shipping" title="Drop shipping">drop shippers</a> or meta sellers. These are members or entities that advertise goods on Amazon who order these goods direct from other competing websites but usually from other Amazon members. These meta sellers may have millions of products listed, have large transaction numbers and are grouped alongside other less prolific members giving them credibility as just someone who has been in business for a long time. Markup is anywhere from 50% to 100% and sometimes more, these sellers maintain that items are in stock when the opposite is true. As Amazon increases their dominance in the marketplace these drop shippers have become more and more commonplace in recent years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In November 2015, Amazon opened a physical Amazon Books store in <a href="/wiki/University_Village,_Seattle" title="University Village, Seattle">University Village</a> in Seattle. The store is 5,500 square feet and prices for all products match those on its website.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-122">[122]</a></sup> Amazon will open its tenth physical book store in 2017;<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> media speculation suggests Amazon plans to eventually roll out 300 to 400 bookstores around the country.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>Amazon plans to open brick and mortar bookstores in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<p>Amazon.com is primarily a retail site with a sales revenue model; Amazon takes a small percentage of the sale price of each item that is sold through its website while also allowing companies to advertise their products by paying to be listed as featured products.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Amazon_(company)&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Amazon.com is ranked 8th on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>For the fiscal year 2018, Amazon reported earnings of US$10.07 billion, with an annual revenue of US$232.887 billion, an increase of 30.9% over the previous fiscal cycle. Since 2007 sales increased from 14.835 billion to 232.887 billion, thanks to continued business expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>Amazon's market capitalization went over US$1 trillion again in early February 2020 after the announcement of the fourth quarter 2019 results.<sup id="cite_ref-4Q_2020_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Q_2020-128">[128]</a></sup> Amazon's total employees now number 798,000. <sup id="cite_ref-4Q_2020_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Q_2020-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
